        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059097097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14478092215058597449"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5510384.Tricks__Tricks___1_' title='Tricks (Tricks, #1) by Ellen Hopkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1347236052s/5510384.jpg' alt='Tricks (Tricks, #1) by Ellen Hopkins' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Wow, I honestly just noticed the amount of pages this book has. I read it in 3 days! I flew through it, because the chapters were so short. Also, I fell in love with Ellen Hopkins' writing style. It was once again confirmed I love these kind of poetic writings. <br/><br/>I have to be honest here: I did like this book, but I forgot what was going on with each of the characters every single time. When I saw their name pop up again, I was like: 'Wait, who was this again?' The characters don't cross paths</span>
  <span id="freeText14478092215058597449" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5510384.Tricks__Tricks___1_" title="Tricks (Tricks, #1) by Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1347236052s/5510384.jpg" alt="Tricks (Tricks, #1) by Ellen Hopkins" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Wow, I honestly just noticed the amount of pages this book has. I read it in 3 days! I flew through it, because the chapters were so short. Also, I fell in love with Ellen Hopkins' writing style. It was once again confirmed I love these kind of poetic writings. <br><br>I have to be honest here: I did like this book, but I forgot what was going on with each of the characters every single time. When I saw their name pop up again, I was like: 'Wait, who was this again?' The characters don't cross paths very much either. The ending of this book did make me tear up, because I found it to be a bit of a happy ending for all of these characters. I know, for sure, I'm not going to pick up the second book in this series. The 'plot' in this book was wrapped up nicely and that will do it for me. A heavy, but certainly worthwhile, read.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3214168694?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="aPriL does feral sometimes " href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes">aPriL does feral sometimes </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416950080" href="/book/show/11339141-tricks">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=unbearably-sad">unbearably-sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=religious-terror">religious-terror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=illuminating">illuminating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=very-very-disturbing-to-me">very-very-disturbing-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=cold-hard-mean">cold-hard-mean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=older-teen">older-teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3214168694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5694640110789768298">'Tricks' by Ellen Hopkins is a very tough read. Five teens end up as prostitutes on the streets of Las Vegas. None of them had a clue that is where they would end up. They are only fifteen to seventeen years old.<br/><br/>Eden Streit's parents are fundamentalist members of the Boise Idaho Assembly of God church. Her father is the minister. They are strict and overbearing. Eden falls in love with the wrong sort of boy - not an Assembly of God member. Andrew and Eden are really truly both in love. When Eden</span>
  <span id="freeText5694640110789768298" style="display:none">'Tricks' by Ellen Hopkins is a very tough read. Five teens end up as prostitutes on the streets of Las Vegas. None of them had a clue that is where they would end up. They are only fifteen to seventeen years old.<br /><br />Eden Streit's parents are fundamentalist members of the Boise Idaho Assembly of God church. Her father is the minister. They are strict and overbearing. Eden falls in love with the wrong sort of boy - not an Assembly of God member. Andrew and Eden are really truly both in love. When Eden's mom figures it out Eden and Andrew have been dating, she sends Eden to a religious concentration camp of sorts for teenagers. It is the type of juvenile institution exactly like a prison - only more starvation. Some of the kids are suspected of being possessed by demons by their parents, like Eden's. One of the attendants will give her more food if she has sex with him. Will he help her escape?<br /><br />Ginger Cordell's mom Iris is one of the worst. She prostitutes herself for money, but calls it having fun, or looking for love. She and her five children live with Ginger's grandmother in California. Iris could get a job. But instead she decides one day to sell her daughter to a customer. Ginger can't take any more of her mother's evil ways.<br /><br />Whitney Lang is the youngest daughter of a wealthy power couple in Santa Cruz. Kyra is their favorite daughter - accomplished, heading for college. Whitney is failing school. Then she falls in love - and the boy ghosts her after taking her virginity. Everyone knows. She is such a loser! First getting drunk at a party seems like a good idea, then she began wondering if anyone cares about her at all. Maybe that guy, Bryn, she met at the mall is the answer. Bryn really seemed to care about her. She will call him.<br /><br />Seth Parnell is gay. He lives in Indiana with his father on a farm. His mother is dead. Both parents hated gay people. When Seth's dad finds out Seth is gay, he tells him to get out of the house and out of his life.<br /><br />Cody Bennett lives in Las Vegas with his mother and stepfather, Jack. He loves both of them. But something is wrong with Jack. Cancer? Money becomes a problem - not enough of it. Cody thinks maybe playing poker will solve the problem. He wins sometimes - but he loses a lot more.<br /><br />These five kids end up in a bad place from a combination of factors. It was very plausible to me how they got there. Teens that are fifteen, sixteen, and seventeen-years-old are not known for their ability to see the forest past the trees! Mixed in with their normal lack of knowledge about people and the wider world, they have few choices and options if they try to be autonomous and support themselves when underage and not very educated or supported by parents. <br /><br />This may sound egocentric, but I clearly remember knowing so much more about resources and outcomes of choices because I read a lot more than my peers as a kid. I still was as dim as burned-out lightbulb about a million other things as my thought processes were one or two dimensional or simply inexperienced; yet, I think my love of reading helped me think better and be able to 'know' certain choices my friends made would not turn out well. The characters in this book were as naive (excepting Ginger) as I saw of my peers about bad things, who also did not read much as well and ended up doing too much emo-driven self-destruction. So, to me, the book is realistic. Of course, I also had crap underclass parents similar to the character Ginger who kneecapped me like Ginger's mother does to Ginger. How can I not recommend this novel?<br /><br />The book is written in free verse. There are some really pretty and poetic descriptions and phrases. But the subject matter is intense whether being about inappropriate sexual teen romances and misfiring teen 'love' relationships, first half of the book, or about the prostitution, last half of the book. The novel is definitely for mature teens and young adults. There are cliffhangers at the end which I presume are wrapped up in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23015872.Traffick__Tricks___2_" title="Traffick (Tricks, #2) by Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Traffick</a>, the sequel to 'Tricks'.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5694640110789768298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I feel so bad for these 5 people who were dealt a horrible hand in life. I m super happy to know there is a second book, due to where this book ends.   <span id="freeText16112759594183236341" style="display:none">For starters there was a lot of people to keep track of and remember the story before the other. I feel so bad for these 5 people who were dealt a horrible hand in life. I m super happy to know there is a second book, due to where this book ends. It dose not have closure which I have to have or I will go crazy. I do not ever what to visit Los Vegas or Reno. Her stories really who what happens on the street, if I were to ever go there I would want to save as many teenagers as I could. My love goes out to the teens who are stuck and can not find away out. Her book not only show the way life can be so hard and how easily you can get trap in the drug life and how men can really mess your life up. Yes I find the books highly recommend to teenagers and adult. One to show girl what some men can be like and how quickly they can take one loves and destroy your innocence. I would want to adult to see what could happen to your child my child, and make them what to do something helpful the next time they see a hooker and ask "What happened and what can I do to help'em?" ( even if they don't want the help) maybe just having that one person show kindness is all it could take.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DQ9tCAfOjLqxDoOhruWAnM2G3+YSbc59cMzfXjQwEwzBbQSxd9rA9SpQjWzlECQaVrF5+A0HwJCopEElyvuYGg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('st5Imh77NuSbH1Oe+2O/kaURggOA4xLj+TzPVdfQ99p+vCEjbu96qwBBXVOwlhsXPiYkHZ+JHA4hVFEuKRt8zA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText7573348682631443186" style="display:none"><i>Ellen Hopkins</i> is the New York Times bestselling author of <i>Crank</i>, <i>Burned</i>, <i>Impulse</i>, <i>Glass</i>, <i>Identical</i>, <i>Tricks</i>, <i>Fallout</i>, <i>Perfect</i>, <i>Triangles</i>, <i>Tilt</i>, and <i>Collateral</i>. She lives in Carson City, Nevada, with her husband and son. Hopkin's Facebook, Twitter, Tumblr and Pinterest pages get thousands of hits from teens who claim Hopkins is the "only one who understands me", and she can be visited at ellenhopkins.com. <br /><br />Like most of you here, books are my life. Reading is a passion, but writing is the biggest part of me. Balance is my greatest challenge, as I love my family, friends, animals and home, but also love traveling to meet my readers. Hope I meet many of you soon!</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/5625827-tricks">Quotes from Tricks</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Some people<br />Never find the right kind of love<br />you know, the kind that steals<br />your breath away.<br />Like diving into a snowmelt.<br />The kind that jolts your heart,<br />sets it beating apace.<br />An anxious hiccuping of hummingbirds wings.<br />The kind that makes every terrible minute apart feel like hours.<br />Days.<br />Years.<br />Some people flit from one insane possibility to the next.<br />Never experincing the connection of two people.<br />rocked by destiny.<br />Never knowing what it means to love someone else,<br />more than themselves.<br />More than life itself, or the promise of something better.<br />Beyond this world,<br />More even (forgive me!) than god.<br />Lucky me, I found the right kind of love.<br />With the wrong person.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/200524-some-people-never-find-the-right-kind-of-love-you">558 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Eyes Tell Stories<br />But do they know how<br />to craft fiction? Do<br />they know how to spin<br />lies?<br />His eyes swear forever,<br />flatter with vows of only<br />me. But are they empty<br />promises?<br />I stare into his eyes, as<br />into a crystal ball, but<br />I cannot find forever,<br />only<br />movies of yesterday,<br />a sketchbook of today,<br />dreams of a shared<br />tomorrow.<br />His eyes whisper secrets.<br />But are they truths or fairy tales?<br />I wonder if even he<br />knows.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/206501-eyes-tell-stories-but-do-they-know-how-to-craft">148 likes</a>
            </nobr>
